href="/wiki/1978_National_League_Championship_Series" title="1978 National League Championship Series">1978</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/1981_National_League_Championship_Series" title="1981 National League Championship Series">1981</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/1988_National_League_Championship_Series" title="1988 National League Championship Series">1988</a></li><li><a League Championship Series">2018</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span style="font-weight:normal;"><b>AA Pennants</b> (1)</span></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/1889_Brooklyn_Bridegrooms_season" title="1889 Brooklyn Bridegrooms season">1889</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">West Division titles <span href="/wiki/2004_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="2004 Los Angeles Dodgers season">2004</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/2008_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="2008 Los Angeles Dodgers season">2008</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/2009_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="2009 Los Angeles Dodgers season">2009</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/2013_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="2013 Los season">2006</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #dcdcdc">Front office</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Owner(s)</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Guggenheim_Baseball_Management" class="mw-redirect" title="Guggenheim Baseball Management">Guggenheim Baseball Management</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Manager</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Dave_Roberts_(outfielder)" title="Dave Roberts (outfielder)">Dave Roberts</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">General Manager</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Farhan_Zaidi" title="Farhan Zaidi">Farhan Zaidi</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">President of Baseball Operations</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Andrew_Friedman" title="Andrew Friedman">Andrew Friedman</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jeff_Pfeffer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Jeff_Pfeffer.jpg/220px-Jeff_Pfeffer.jpg" width="220" height="287" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2a/Jeff_Pfeffer.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="253" data-file-height="330" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jeff_Pfeffer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jeff_Pfeffer" title="Jeff Pfeffer">Jeff Pfeffer</a>, 1916 Brooklyn Robins</div></div></div>\n<p>The <b>Los Angeles Dodgers</b> are an American professional <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> team based in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles, California</a>. The Dodgers compete in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB) as a member club of the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> (NL) <a href="/wiki/National_League_West" title="National League West">West</a> division. Established in 1883 in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>, New York,<sup id="cite_ref-National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LeonardBernardo_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeonardBernardo-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> the team <a href="/wiki/Relocation_of_professional_sports_teams" title="Relocation of professional sports teams">moved</a> to Los Angeles before the 1958 season.<sup id="cite_ref-DodgersTimeline1950s_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DodgersTimeline1950s-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> They played for four seasons at the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Memorial_Coliseum" title="Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum">Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum</a> before moving to their current home of <a href="/wiki/Dodger_Stadium" title="Dodger Stadium">Dodger Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/1962_in_baseball" title="1962 in baseball">1962</a>.\n</p><p>The Dodgers as a franchise have won six <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Series_champions" title="List of World Series champions">World Series</a> titles and 23 <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_League_pennant_winners" title="List of National League pennant winners">National League pennants</a>. 11 <a href="/wiki/National_League_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="National League Most Valuable Player Award">NL MVP award</a> winners have played for the Dodgers, winning a total of 13 MVP Awards, Eight <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Award</a> winners have pitched for the Dodgers, winning a total of twelve Cy Young Awards. The team has also produced 18 <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Rookie_of_the_Year_Award" title="Major League Baseball Rookie of the Year Award">Rookie of the Year Award</a> winners, twice as many as the next closest team, including four consecutive from 1979 to 1982 and five consecutive from 1992 to 1996.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In the early 20th century, the team, then known as the Robins, won league pennants in <a href="/wiki/1916_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1916 Major League Baseball season">1916</a> and <a href="/wiki/1920_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1920 Major League Baseball season">1920</a>, losing the World Series both times, first to <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston</a> and then <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland</a>. In the 1930s, the team changed its name to the Dodgers, named after the Brooklyn pedestrians who dodged the streetcars in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In 1941, the Dodgers captured their third <a href="/wiki/National_League_pennant" class="mw-redirect" title="National League pennant">National League pennant</a>, only to lose to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>. This marked the onset of the <a href="/wiki/Dodgers%E2%80%93Yankees_rivalry" title="Dodgers\xe2\x80\x93Yankees rivalry">Dodgers\xe2\x80\x93Yankees rivalry</a>, as the Dodgers would face them in their next six <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> appearances. Led by <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a>, the first black Major League Baseball player of the modern era; and three-time National League Most Valuable Player <a href="/wiki/Roy_Campanella" title="Roy Campanella">Roy Campanella</a>, also signed out of the Negro Leagues, the Dodgers captured their first <a href="/wiki/1955_World_Series" title="1955 World Series">World Series title in 1955</a> by defeating the Yankees for the first time, a story notably described in the 1972 book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boys_of_Summer_(book)" title="The Boys of Summer (book)">The Boys of Summer</a></i>.\n</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/1957_Brooklyn_Dodgers_season" title="1957 Brooklyn Dodgers season">1957 season</a> the team left Brooklyn. In just their second season in Los Angeles, the Dodgers won their second World Series title, beating the Chicago White Sox in six games in 1959. Spearheaded by the dominant pitching style of <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Koufax" title="Sandy Koufax">Sandy Koufax</a> and <a href="/wiki/Don_Drysdale" title="Don Drysdale">Don Drysdale</a>, the Dodgers captured three pennants in the 1960s and won two more World Series titles, sweeping the Yankees in four games in 1963, and edging the Minnesota Twins in seven in 1965. The 1963 sweep was their second victory against the Yankees, and their first against them as a Los Angeles team. The Dodgers won four more pennants in 1966, 1974, 1977 and 1978, but lost in each World Series appearance. They went on to win the World Series again in 1981, thanks in part to pitching sensation <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Valenzuela" title="Fernando Valenzuela">Fernando Valenzuela</a>. The early 1980s were affectionately dubbed "Fernandomania." In 1988, another pitching hero, <a href="/wiki/Orel_Hershiser" title="Orel Hershiser">Orel Hershiser</a>, again led them to a World Series victory, aided by one of the most memorable home runs of all time, by their injured star outfielder <a href="/wiki/Kirk_Gibson" title="Kirk Gibson">Kirk Gibson</a> coming off the bench to pinch hit with two outs in the bottom of the ninth inning of game 1, in his only appearance of the series. The Dodgers won the pennant in 2017, but lost the World Series to the Houston Astros. \n</p><p>The Dodgers share a fierce <a href="/wiki/Dodgers%E2%80%93Giants_rivalry" title="Dodgers\xe2\x80\x93Giants rivalry">rivalry</a> with the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a>, the oldest rivalry in baseball, dating back to when the two franchises played in New York City. Both teams moved west for the 1958 season. The Brooklyn Dodgers and Los Angeles Dodgers have collectively appeared in the World Series 20 times, while the New York Giants and San Francisco Giants have also collectively appeared 20 times. The Giants have won two more World Series (8); the Dodgers and Giants share the record of 23 National League Pennants. Although the two franchises have enjoyed near equal success, the city rivalries are rather lopsided and in both cases, a team\'s championships have predated to the other\'s first one in that particular location. When the two teams were based in New York, the Giants won five World Series championships, and the Dodgers one. After the move to California, the Dodgers have won five in Los Angeles, the Giants have won three in San Francisco.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_history">Team history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Team history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brooklyn_Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Brooklyn Dodgers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Brooklyn_Dodgers" title="History of the Brooklyn Dodgers">History of the Brooklyn Dodgers</a></div>\n<p>The Dodgers were founded in 1883 as the <b>Brooklyn Atlantics</b>, taking the name of a <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Atlantics" title="Brooklyn Atlantics">defunct team</a> that had played in Brooklyn before them. The team joined the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_(19th_century)" title="American Association (19th century)">American Association</a> in 1884 and won the AA championship in 1889 before joining the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> in 1890. They promptly won the NL Championship their first year in the League. The team was known alternatively as the <b>Bridegrooms</b><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><b>, Grooms, Superbas, Robins</b>, and <b>Trolley Dodgers</b> before officially becoming the <b>Dodgers</b> in the 1930s.\n</p><p>In Brooklyn, the Dodgers won the NL pennant several times (<a href="/wiki/1890_Brooklyn_Bridegrooms_season" title="1890 Brooklyn Bridegrooms season">1890</a>, <a href="/wiki/1899_Brooklyn_Superbas_season" title="1899 Brooklyn Superbas season">1899</a>, <a href="/wiki/1900_Brooklyn_Superbas_season" title="1900 Brooklyn Superbas season">1900</a>, <a href="/wiki/1916_Brooklyn_Robins_season" title="1916 Brooklyn Robins season">1916</a>, <a href="/wiki/1920_Brooklyn_Robins_season" title="1920 Brooklyn Robins season">1920</a>, <a href="/wiki/1941_Brooklyn_Dodgers_season" title="1941 Brooklyn Dodgers season">1941</a>, <a href="/wiki/1947_Brooklyn_Dodgers_season" title="1947 Brooklyn Dodgers season">1947</a>, <a href="/wiki/1949_Brooklyn_Dodgers_season" title="1949 Brooklyn Dodgers season">1949</a>, <a href="/wiki/1952_Brooklyn_Dodgers_season" title="1952 Brooklyn Dodgers season">1952</a>, <a href="/wiki/1953_Brooklyn_Dodgers_season" title="1953 Brooklyn Dodgers season">1953</a>, <a href="/wiki/1955_Brooklyn_Dodgers_season" title="1955 Brooklyn Dodgers season">1955</a>, <a href="/wiki/1956_Brooklyn_Dodgers_season" title="1956 Brooklyn Dodgers season">1956</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> in <a href="/wiki/1955_World_Series" title="1955 World Series">1955</a>. After moving to Los Angeles, the team won National League pennants in <a href="/wiki/1959_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1959 Los Angeles Dodgers season">1959</a>, <a href="/wiki/1963_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1963 Los Angeles Dodgers season">1963</a>, <a href="/wiki/1965_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1965 Los Angeles Dodgers season">1965</a>, <a href="/wiki/1966_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1966 Los Angeles Dodgers season">1966</a>, <a href="/wiki/1974_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1974 Los Angeles Dodgers season">1974</a>, <a href="/wiki/1977_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1977 Los Angeles Dodgers season">1977</a>, <a href="/wiki/1978_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1978 Los Angeles Dodgers season">1978</a>, <a href="/wiki/1981_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1981 Los Angeles Dodgers season">1981</a>, <a href="/wiki/1988_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1988 Los Angeles Dodgers season">1988</a>, <a href="/wiki/2017_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="2017 Los Angeles Dodgers season">2017</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2018_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="2018 Los Angeles Dodgers season">2018</a>, with World Series championships in <a href="/wiki/1959_World_Series" title="1959 World Series">1959</a>, <a href="/wiki/1963_World_Series" title="1963 World Series">1963</a>, <a href="/wiki/1965_World_Series" title="1965 World Series">1965</a>, <a href="/wiki/1981_World_Series" title="1981 World Series">1981</a> and <a href="/wiki/1988_World_Series" title="1988 World Series">1988</a>. In all, the Dodgers have appeared in 20 World Series: 9 in Brooklyn and 11 in Los Angeles.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jackie_Robinson">Jackie Robinson</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Jackie Robinson">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a></div>\n<p>For most of the first half of the 20th century, no Major League Baseball team employed an African American player. <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a> became the first African American to play for a Major League Baseball team when he played his first major league game on April 15, 1947, as a member of the Brooklyn Dodgers. This was mainly due to general manager <a href="/wiki/Branch_Rickey" title="Branch Rickey">Branch Rickey</a>\'s efforts. The deeply religious Rickey\'s motivation appears to have been primarily moral, although business considerations were also a factor. Rickey was a member of <a href="/wiki/The_Methodist_Church_(USA)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Methodist Church (USA)">The Methodist Church</a>, the antecedent denomination to <a href="/wiki/The_United_Methodist_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="The United Methodist Church">The United Methodist Church</a> of today, which was a strong advocate for <a href="/wiki/Social_justice" title="Social justice">social justice</a> and active later in the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_Rights_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="American Civil Rights Movement">American Civil Rights Movement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-&#91;&#91;The_New_York_Times&#93;&#93;_-_Branch_Rickey_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-[[The_New_York_Times]]_-_Branch_Rickey-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>This event was the harbinger of the integration of professional sports in the United States, the concomitant demise of the <a href="/wiki/Negro_league_baseball" title="Negro league baseball">Negro Leagues</a>, and is regarded as a key moment in the history of the American Civil Rights movement. Robinson was an exceptional player, a speedy <a href="/wiki/Stolen_base" title="Stolen base">runner</a> who sparked the team with his intensity. He was the inaugural recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Rookie_of_the_Year_Award" title="Major League Baseball Rookie of the Year Award">Rookie of the Year</a> award, which is now named the Jackie Robinson Award in his honor. The Dodgers\' willingness to integrate, when most other teams refused to, was a key factor in their 1947\xe2\x80\x931956 success. They won six pennants in those 10 years with the help of Robinson, three-time MVP <a href="/wiki/Roy_Campanella" title="Roy Campanella">Roy Campanella</a>, Cy Young Award winner <a href="/wiki/Don_Newcombe" title="Don Newcombe">Don Newcombe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Gilliam" title="Jim Gilliam">Jim Gilliam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Black" title="Joe Black">Joe Black</a>. Robinson would eventually go on to become the first African-American elected to the <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Baseball Hall of Fame">Baseball Hall of Fame</a> in 1962.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Move_to_Los_Angeles">Move to Los Angeles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Move to Los Angeles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dodgers_Greats.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Dodgers_Greats.JPG/220px-Dodgers_Greats.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Dodgers_Greats.JPG/330px-Dodgers_Greats.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Dodgers_Greats.JPG/440px-Dodgers_Greats.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dodgers_Greats.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former Dodger greats who played in both Brooklyn and Los Angeles adorn the exterior of <a href="/wiki/Dodger_Stadium" title="Dodger Stadium">Dodger Stadium</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Real estate businessman <a href="/wiki/Walter_O%27Malley" title="Walter O&#39;Malley">Walter O\'Malley</a> acquired majority ownership of the Dodgers in 1950, when he bought the 25 percent share of co-owner <a href="/wiki/Branch_Rickey" title="Branch Rickey">Branch Rickey</a> and became allied with the widow of the another equal partner, <a href="/wiki/John_L._Smith_(pharmaceutical_executive)" title="John L. Smith (pharmaceutical executive)">Mrs. John L. Smith</a>. Before long, he was working to buy new land in Brooklyn to build a more accessible and better arrayed ballpark than <a href="/wiki/Ebbets_Field" title="Ebbets Field">Ebbets Field</a>. Beloved as it was, Ebbets Field was no longer well-served by its aging infrastructure and the Dodgers could no longer sell out the park even in the heat of a pennant race, despite largely dominating the National League from 1946 to 1957.\n</p><p>O\'Malley wanted to build a <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Dodgers_proposed_domed_stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Dodgers proposed domed stadium">new, state of the art stadium in Brooklyn</a>. But City Planner <a href="/wiki/Robert_Moses" title="Robert Moses">Robert Moses</a> and New York politicians refused to grant him the eminent domain authority required to build pursuant to O\'Malley\'s plans. To put pressure on the city, during the 1955 season, O\'Malley announced that the team would play seven regular season games and one exhibition game at Jersey City\'s <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Stadium" title="Roosevelt Stadium">Roosevelt Stadium</a> in 1956.<sup id="cite_ref-Jersey_City_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jersey_City-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Moses and the City considered this an empty threat, and did not believe O\'Malley would go through with moving the team from New York City.\n</p><p>After teams began to travel to and from games by air instead of train, it became possible to include locations in the far west. Los Angeles officials attended the <a href="/wiki/1956_World_Series" title="1956 World Series">1956 World Series</a> looking to the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Washington_Senators" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Washington Senators">Washington Senators</a> to move to the West Coast. When O\'Malley heard that LA was looking for a club, he sent word to the Los Angeles officials that he was interested in talking. LA offered him what New York would not: a chance to buy land suitable for building a ballpark, and own that ballpark, giving him complete control over all revenue streams. When the news came out, NYC Mayor <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Wagner,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Robert F. Wagner, Jr.">Robert F. Wagner, Jr.</a> and Moses made an offer to build a ballpark on the World\'s Fair Grounds in <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a> that would be shared by the Giants and Dodgers. However, O\'Malley was interested in his park only under his conditions, and the plans for a new stadium in Brooklyn seemed like a pipe dream. O\'Malley decided to move the Dodgers to California, convincing Giants owner <a href="/wiki/Horace_Stoneham" title="Horace Stoneham">Horace Stoneham</a> to move to San Francisco instead of Minneapolis to keep another team on the West Coast to ease approval of the moves. There was no turning back: the Dodgers were heading for Hollywood.<sup id="cite_ref-Jersey_City_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jersey_City-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Dodgers played their final game at <a href="/wiki/Ebbets_Field" title="Ebbets Field">Ebbets Field</a> on September 24, 1957, which the <a href="/wiki/1957_Brooklyn_Dodgers_season" title="1957 Brooklyn Dodgers season">Dodgers</a> won 2\xe2\x80\x930 over the <a href="/wiki/1957_Pittsburgh_Pirates_season" title="1957 Pittsburgh Pirates season">Pittsburgh Pirates</a>.\n</p><p>New York would remain a one-team town with the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> until 1962, when Joan Payson founded the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a> and brought National League baseball back to the city. The blue background used by the Dodgers, would be adopted by the Mets, honoring their New York NL forebears with a blend of Dodgers blue and Giants orange.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Los_Angeles_Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Los Angeles Dodgers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="History of the Los Angeles Dodgers">History of the Los Angeles Dodgers</a></div>\n<p>The Dodgers were the first Major League Baseball team to ever play in Los Angeles. On April 18, 1958, the Dodgers played their first LA game, defeating the former New York and now new <a href="/wiki/1958_San_Francisco_Giants_season" title="1958 San Francisco Giants season">San Francisco Giants</a>, 6\xe2\x80\x935, before 78,672 fans at the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Memorial_Coliseum" title="Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum">Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum</a>. Catcher <a href="/wiki/Roy_Campanella" title="Roy Campanella">Roy Campanella</a>, left partially paralyzed in an off-season accident, was never able to play in Los Angeles.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LA_Coliseum_1959_World_Series.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/LA_Coliseum_1959_World_Series.jpg/220px-LA_Coliseum_1959_World_Series.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/LA_Coliseum_1959_World_Series.jpg/330px-LA_Coliseum_1959_World_Series.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/LA_Coliseum_1959_World_Series.jpg/440px-LA_Coliseum_1959_World_Series.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3400" data-file-height="2328" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LA_Coliseum_1959_World_Series.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/1959_World_Series" title="1959 World Series">1959 World Series</a> was played partially at the <a href="/wiki/LA_Coliseum" class="mw-redirect" title="LA Coliseum">LA Coliseum</a> while Dodger Stadium was being built.</div></div></div>\n<p>Construction on <a href="/wiki/Dodger_Stadium" title="Dodger Stadium">Dodger Stadium</a> was completed in time for Opening Day 1962. With its clean, simple lines and its picturesque setting amid hills and palm trees, the ballpark quickly became an icon of the Dodgers and their new California lifestyle. O\'Malley was determined that there would not be a bad seat in the house, achieving this by <a href="/wiki/Cantilever" title="Cantilever">cantilevered</a> grandstands that have since been widely imitated. More importantly for the team, the stadium\'s spacious dimensions, along with other factors, gave defense an advantage over offense and the Dodgers moved to take advantage of this by assembling a team that would excel with its <a href="/wiki/Pitch_(baseball)" title="Pitch (baseball)">pitching</a>.\n</p><p>Since moving to Los Angeles, the Dodgers have won 11 more National League Championships and five <a href="/wiki/World_Series_ring" title="World Series ring">World Series rings</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_historical_notes">Other historical notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Other historical notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_records_and_firsts">Historical records and firsts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Historical records and firsts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>First baseball team to win championships in different leagues in consecutive years (1889\xe2\x80\x931890)</li>\n<li>First television broadcast (1939)</li>\n<li>First use of batting helmets (1941)</li>\n<li>First MLB team to employ and start an African-American player in the 20th century (<a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a>, 1947)</li>\n<li>First MLB team to have numbers on the front of their uniforms (1952)</li>\n<li>First West Coast team (1958) \xe2\x80\x93 along with the San Francisco Giants</li>\n<li>First MLB team to allow a female sports journalist into a locker room (<a href="/wiki/Anita_Martini" title="Anita Martini">Anita Martini</a>, 1974)</li>\n<li>Largest home-opener attendance: 78,672 (1958) (since broken by the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a> in 1993)</li>\n<li>Largest single game attendance: 93,103 (1959) and 115,300 (2008) *World Record</li>\n<li>First MLB team to open an office in Asia (1998)</li>\n<li>Longest MLB record for home start going 13\xe2\x80\x930 (2009)</li>\n<li>North American record for the buying of a sports team ($2 billion, 2012)</li>\n<li>First MLB team to employ a female lead trainer (Sue Falsone, 2012)</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin_of_the_nickname">Origin of the nickname</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Origin of the nickname">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Dodgers\' official history reports that the term "Trolley Dodgers" was attached to the Brooklyn ballclub due to the complex maze of trolley cars that weaved its way through the borough of Brooklyn.<sup id="cite_ref-DodgersTimeline1890s_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DodgersTimeline1890s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1892, the city of Brooklyn (Brooklyn was an independent city until annexed by New York City in 1898) began replacing its slow-moving, horse-drawn trolley lines with the faster, more powerful electric trolley lines.<sup id="cite_ref-Brown_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Within less than three years, by the end of 1895, electric trolley accidents in Brooklyn had resulted in more than 130 deaths and maimed well over 500 people.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Brooklyn\'s high profile, the significant number of widely reported accidents, and a trolley strike in early 1895, combined to create a strong association in the public\'s mind between Brooklyn and trolley dodging.<sup id="cite_ref-Brown_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sportswriters started using the name "trolley dodgers" to refer to the Brooklyn team early in the 1895 season.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The name was shortened to, on occasion, the "Brooklyn Dodgers" as early as 1898.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sportswriters in the early 20th century began referring to the Dodgers as the "Bums", in reference to the team\'s fans and possibly because of the "street character" nature of Jack Dawkins, the "Artful Dodger" in Charles Dickens\' <i>Oliver Twist</i>. Newspaper cartoonist <a href="/wiki/Willard_Mullin" title="Willard Mullin">Willard Mullin</a> used a drawing of famous clown <a href="/wiki/Emmett_Kelly" title="Emmett Kelly">Emmett Kelly</a> to depict "Dem Bums": the team would later use "Weary Willie" in promotional images, and Kelly himself was a club mascot during the 1950s.\n</p><p>Other team names used by the franchise were the Atlantics, Grays, Grooms, Bridegrooms, Superbas and Robins. All of these nicknames were used by fans and sportswriters to describe the team, but not in any official capacity. The team\'s legal name was the Brooklyn Base Ball Club.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> However, the Trolley Dodger nickname was used throughout this period, simultaneously with these other nicknames, by fans and sportswriters of the day. The team did not use the name in any formal sense until 1932, when the word "Dodgers" appeared on team jerseys.<sup id="cite_ref-National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The "conclusive shift" came in 1933, when both home and road jerseys for the team bore the name "Dodgers".<sup id="cite_ref-LeonardBernardo_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeonardBernardo-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Examples of how the many popularized names of the team were used are available from newspaper articles before 1932. A New York Times article describing a game in 1916 starts out: "Jimmy Callahan, pilot of the Pirates, did his best to wreck the hopes the Dodgers have of gaining the National League pennant", but then goes on to comment: "the only thing that saved the Superbas from being toppled from first place was that the Phillies lost one of the two games played".<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> What is interesting about the use of these two nicknames is that most baseball statistics sites and baseball historians generally now refer to the pennant-winning 1916 Brooklyn team as the Robins. A 1918 New York Times article uses the nickname in its title: "Buccaneers Take Last From Robins", but the subtitle of the article reads: "Subdue The Superbas By 11 To 4, Making Series An Even Break".<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another example of the use of the many nicknames is found on the program issued at Ebbets Field for the <a href="/wiki/1920_World_Series" title="1920 World Series">1920 World Series</a>, which identifies the matchup in the series as "Dodgers vs. Indians" despite the fact that the Robins nickname had been in consistent use for around six years.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The "Robins" nickname was derived from the name of their Hall of Fame manager, Wilbert Robinson, who led the team from 1914 to 1931.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uniforms">Uniforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Uniforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dodgersuni.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Dodgersuni.png/220px-Dodgersuni.png" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Dodgersuni.png/330px-Dodgersuni.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Dodgersuni.png/440px-Dodgersuni.png 2x" data-file-width="927" data-file-height="625" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dodgersuni.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Dodgers\' home uniform has remained relatively unchanged for 70 years.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Dodgers\' uniform has remained relatively unchanged since the 1930s. The home jersey is white with "Dodgers" written in script across the chest in royal. The road jersey is gray with "Los Angeles" written in script across the chest in royal. The word "Dodgers" was first used on the front of the team\'s home jersey in 1933; the uniform was then white with red pinstripes and a stylized "B" on the left shoulder.<sup id="cite_ref-DodgersUniformsLogos_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DodgersUniformsLogos-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The Dodgers also wore green outlined uniforms and green caps throughout the 1937 season but reverted to blue the following year.\n</p><p>The current design was created in 1939, and has remained the same ever since with only cosmetic changes. In 1952, the home uniform added a red uniform number under the "Dodgers" script. The road jersey also has a red uniform number under the script. When the franchise moved from Brooklyn to Los Angeles, the city name on the road jersey changed, and the stylized "B" was replaced with the interlocking "LA" on the caps in 1958. In 1970, the Dodgers removed the city name from the road jerseys and had "Dodgers" on both the home and away uniforms. The city script returned to the road jerseys in 1999, and the tradition-rich Dodgers flirted with an alternate uniform for the first time since 1944 (when all-blue satin uniforms were introduced). These 1999 alternate jerseys had a royal top with the "Dodgers" script in white across the chest, and the red number on the front. These were worn with white pants and a new cap with silver brim, top button and Dodger logo. These alternates proved unpopular and the team abandoned them after only one season. In 2014, the Dodgers introduced an alternate road jersey: a gray version with the "Dodgers" script instead of the city name.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, the Dodgers will be wearing their 60th anniversary patch to honor the 60 years of being in Los Angeles.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Los_Angeles_Dodgers_Logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/20/Los_Angeles_Dodgers_Logo.png/114px-Los_Angeles_Dodgers_Logo.png" width="114" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/20/Los_Angeles_Dodgers_Logo.png/171px-Los_Angeles_Dodgers_Logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/20/Los_Angeles_Dodgers_Logo.png/228px-Los_Angeles_Dodgers_Logo.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="316" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Current logo using "Dodgers" Script\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:47.5px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Los_Angeles_Dodgers_Script_Logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Los_Angeles_Dodgers_Script_Logo.svg/120px-Los_Angeles_Dodgers_Script_Logo.svg.png" width="120" height="55" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Los_Angeles_Dodgers_Script_Logo.svg/180px-Los_Angeles_Dodgers_Script_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Los_Angeles_Dodgers_Script_Logo.svg/240px-Los_Angeles_Dodgers_Script_Logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="50" data-file-height="23" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Los Angeles Dodgers Script on Dodger Blue\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asian_players">Asian players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Asian players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DSC03270_Chan_Ho_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/DSC03270_Chan_Ho_Park.jpg/170px-DSC03270_Chan_Ho_Park.jpg" width="170" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/DSC03270_Chan_Ho_Park.jpg/255px-DSC03270_Chan_Ho_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/DSC03270_Chan_Ho_Park.jpg/340px-DSC03270_Chan_Ho_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2329" data-file-height="3226" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DSC03270_Chan_Ho_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chan_Ho_Park" title="Chan Ho Park">Chan Ho Park</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Dodgers have been groundbreaking in their signing of players from Asia; mainly, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>. Former owner <a href="/wiki/Peter_O%27Malley" title="Peter O&#39;Malley">Peter O\'Malley</a> began reaching out in 1980 by starting clinics in China and South Korea, building baseball fields in two Chinese cities, and in 1998 becoming the first major league team to open an office in Asia. The Dodgers were the second team to start a Japanese player in recent history, pitcher <a href="/wiki/Hideo_Nomo" title="Hideo Nomo">Hideo Nomo</a>, the first team to start a South Korean player, pitcher <a href="/wiki/Chan_Ho_Park" title="Chan Ho Park">Chan Ho Park</a>, and the first Taiwanese player, <a href="/wiki/Chin-Feng_Chen" class="mw-redirect" title="Chin-Feng Chen">Chin-Feng Chen</a>. In addition, they were the first team to send out three Asian pitchers, from different Asian countries, in one game: Park, <a href="/wiki/Hong-Chih_Kuo" title="Hong-Chih Kuo">Hong-Chih Kuo</a> of Taiwan, and <a href="/wiki/Takashi_Saito_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Takashi Saito (baseball)">Takashi Saito</a> of Japan. In the 2008 season, the Dodgers had the most Asian players on its roster of any major league team with five. They included Japanese pitchers <a href="/wiki/Takashi_Saito_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Takashi Saito (baseball)">Takashi Saito</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hiroki_Kuroda" title="Hiroki Kuroda">Hiroki Kuroda</a>; South Korean pitcher <a href="/wiki/Chan_Ho_Park" title="Chan Ho Park">Chan Ho Park</a>; and Taiwanese pitcher <a href="/wiki/Hong-Chih_Kuo" title="Hong-Chih Kuo">Hong-Chih Kuo</a> and infielder <a href="/wiki/Chin-Lung_Hu" class="mw-redirect" title="Chin-Lung Hu">Chin-Lung Hu</a>. In 2005, the Dodgers\' <a href="/wiki/Hee_Seop_Choi" class="mw-redirect" title="Hee Seop Choi">Hee Seop Choi</a> became the first Asian player to compete in the <a href="/wiki/Home_Run_Derby" title="Home Run Derby">Home Run Derby</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> For the 2013 season, the Dodgers signed starting pitcher <a href="/wiki/Hyun-Jin_Ryu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyun-Jin Ryu">Hyun-Jin Ryu</a> with a six-year, $36 million contract, after posting a bid of nearly $27 million to acquire him from the <a href="/wiki/Korea_Baseball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Korea Baseball Championship">KBO</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Hanhwa_Eagles" class="mw-redirect" title="Hanhwa Eagles">Hanhwa Eagles</a>. For the 2016 season, the Dodgers signed starting pitcher <a href="/wiki/Kenta_Maeda" title="Kenta Maeda">Kenta Maeda</a> with an eight-year, $25 million contract, after posting a bid of $20 million to acquire him from the <a href="/wiki/Nippon_Professional_Baseball" title="Nippon Professional Baseball">NPB</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Hiroshima_Toyo_Carp" title="Hiroshima Toyo Carp">Hiroshima Toyo Carp</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Dodgers\' rivalry with the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> dates back to the 19th century, when the two teams were based in New York; the rivalry with the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> took place when the Dodgers were based in New York, but was revived with their East Coast/West Coast World Series battles in 1963, 1977, 1978, and 1981. The Dodgers rivalry with the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a> also dates back to their days in New York, but was most fierce during the 1970s, 1980s, and 2000s. The Dodgers also had a heated rivalry with the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a> during the 1970s, 1980s and early 1990s. The rivalry with the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels_of_Anaheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim">Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim</a> and the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a> dates back to the Angels\' and Padres\' respective inaugural seasons (Angels in 1961, Padres in 1969). Regional proximity is behind the rivalries with both the Angels and the Padres.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="San_Francisco_Giants">San Francisco Giants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: San Francisco Giants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dodgers%E2%80%93Giants_rivalry" title="Dodgers\xe2\x80\x93Giants rivalry">Dodgers\xe2\x80\x93Giants rivalry</a></div>\n<p>The Dodgers\xe2\x80\x93Giants rivalry is one of the longest-standing rivalries in American baseball.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The feud between the Dodgers and the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> began in the late 19th century when both clubs were based in New York City, with the Dodgers playing in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a> and the Giants playing at the <a href="/wiki/Polo_Grounds" title="Polo Grounds">Polo Grounds</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>. After the 1957 season, Dodgers owner <a href="/wiki/Walter_O%27Malley" title="Walter O&#39;Malley">Walter O\'Malley</a> moved the team to Los Angeles for financial and other reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-MoveToCalifornia_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoveToCalifornia-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Along the way, he managed to convince Giants owner <a href="/wiki/Horace_Stoneham" title="Horace Stoneham">Horace Stoneham</a>\xe2\x80\x94who was considering moving his team to <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">Minnesota</a>\xe2\x80\x94to preserve the rivalry by bringing his team to California as well.<sup id="cite_ref-MoveToCalifornia_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoveToCalifornia-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_New_York_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Sports in New York City">New York</a> baseball fans were stunned and heartbroken by the move.<sup id="cite_ref-MoveToCalifornia_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoveToCalifornia-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Given that the cities of Los Angeles and San Francisco have been bitter rivals in economic, cultural, and political arenas for over a century and a half, the new venue in California became fertile ground for its transplantation.\n</p><p>Each team\'s ability to endure for over a century while moving across an entire continent, as well as the rivalry\'s leap from a cross-city to a cross-state engagement, have led to the rivalry being considered one of the greatest in American sports history.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Unlike many other historic baseball match-ups in which one team remains dominant for most of their history, the Dodgers\xe2\x80\x93Giants rivalry has exhibited a persistent balance in the respective successes of the two teams. While the Giants have more wins in franchise history, the Dodgers and Giants are tied for most National League Pennants at 23, though the Giants have won eight <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> titles, while the Dodgers have won six.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The <a href="/wiki/2010_World_Series" title="2010 World Series">2010 World Series</a> was the Giants\' first championship since moving to California, while the Dodgers had won five World Series titles since their move, their last title coming in the <a href="/wiki/1988_World_Series" title="1988 World Series">1988 World Series</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Los_Angeles_Angels_of_Anaheim">Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Freeway_Series" title="Freeway Series">Freeway Series</a></div>\n<p>This rivalry refers to a series of games played with the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels" title="Los Angeles Angels">Los Angeles Angels</a>. The Freeway Series takes its name from the massive freeway system in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Los_Angeles_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Los Angeles Area">greater Los Angeles metropolitan area</a>, the home of both teams; one could travel from one team\'s stadium to the other simply by traveling along <a href="/wiki/Interstate_5" title="Interstate 5">Interstate 5</a>. The term is akin to <i><a href="/wiki/Subway_Series" title="Subway Series">Subway Series</a></i> which refers to meetings between New York City baseball teams. The term "<i>Freeway Series</i>" also inspired the official name of the regions\' <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">NHL</a> rivalry: the <i><a href="/wiki/Freeway_Face-Off" title="Freeway Face-Off">Freeway Face-Off</a></i>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_rivalry">Historical rivalry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Historical rivalry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_York_Yankees">New York Yankees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: New York Yankees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Dodgers%E2%80%93Yankees_rivalry" title="Dodgers\xe2\x80\x93Yankees rivalry">Dodgers\xe2\x80\x93Yankees rivalry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Subway_Series" title="Subway Series">Subway Series</a></div>\n<p>The Dodgers\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">Yankees</a> rivalry is one of the most well-known <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_rivalries" title="Major League Baseball rivalries">rivalries in Major League Baseball</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-YankeesDodgers_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YankeesDodgers-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The two teams have met eleven times in the <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a>, more times than any other pair from the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National Leagues</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-YankeesDodgers_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YankeesDodgers-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The initial significance was embodied in the two teams\' proximity in New York City, when the Dodgers initially played in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>. After the Dodgers moved to Los Angeles in 1958, the rivalry retained its significance as the two teams represented the dominant cities on each coast of the United States, and <a href="/wiki/Largest_cities_in_the_United_States_by_population_by_decade" class="mw-redirect" title="Largest cities in the United States by population by decade">since the 1980s</a>, the two largest cities in the United States.\n</p><p>Although the rivalry\'s significance arose from the two teams\' numerous World Series meetings,<sup id="cite_ref-YankeesDodgers_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YankeesDodgers-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> the Yankees and Dodgers have not met in the World Series since <a href="/wiki/1981_World_Series" title="1981 World Series">1981</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-YankeesDodgers_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YankeesDodgers-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> They would not play each other in a non-exhibition game until 2004, when they played a three-game <a href="/wiki/Interleague_play" title="Interleague play">interleague</a> series.<sup id="cite_ref-YankeesDodgers_33-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YankeesDodgers-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Their last meeting was in September 2016, when the Dodgers won two out of three games in New York.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fan_support">Fan support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Fan support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MLB_playoffs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/MLB_playoffs.jpg/170px-MLB_playoffs.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/MLB_playoffs.jpg/255px-MLB_playoffs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/MLB_playoffs.jpg/340px-MLB_playoffs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="453" data-file-height="604" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MLB_playoffs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A fan waves a <a href="/wiki/Rally_towel" title="Rally towel">rally towel</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2008_National_League_Championship_Series" title="2008 National League Championship Series">2008 National League Championship Series (NLCS)</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Dodgers have a loyal fanbase, evidenced by the fact that the Dodgers were the first MLB team to attract more than 3 million fans in a season (in 1978), and accomplished that feat six more times before any other franchise did it once.<sup id="cite_ref-ballparksofbaseball.com_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ballparksofbaseball.com-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The Dodgers drew at least 3 million fans for 15 consecutive seasons from 1996 to 2010, the longest such streak in all of MLB.<sup id="cite_ref-ballparksofbaseball.com_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ballparksofbaseball.com-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> On July 3, 2007, Dodgers management announced that total franchise attendance, dating back to 1901, had reached 175&#160;million, a record for all professional sports.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, the Dodgers set a franchise record for single-season attendance, attracting over 3.8&#160;million fans.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, the Dodgers led MLB in total attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The Dodger baseball cap is consistently in the top three in sales.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> During the 2011\xe2\x80\x932012 season, <a href="/wiki/Frank_McCourt_(executive)" title="Frank McCourt (executive)">Frank McCourt</a>, the owner of the Dodgers at that time, was going through a rough divorce with his wife over who should be the owner of the Dodger team. Instead, Frank McCourt paid $131 million to his wife as part of the divorce settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> As a result, the team payroll was financially low for a big-budget team crippling the Dodgers in the free-agent market. Collectively, the team performance waned due to the distracting drama in the front office resulting in low attendance numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Given the team\'s proximity to Hollywood, numerous celebrities can often be seen attending home games at Dodger Stadium. Celebrities such as co-owner <a href="/wiki/Magic_Johnson" title="Magic Johnson">Magic Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Hart" title="Mary Hart">Mary Hart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Larry_King" title="Larry King">Larry King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Woods" title="Tiger Woods">Tiger Woods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alyssa_Milano" title="Alyssa Milano">Alyssa Milano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shia_LaBeouf" title="Shia LaBeouf">Shia LaBeouf</a> are known to sit at field box seats behind home plate where they sign autographs for fellow Dodger fans. Actor <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Cranston" title="Bryan Cranston">Bryan Cranston</a> is a lifelong Dodger fan.\n</p><p>The Dodgers set the world record for the largest attendance for a single baseball game during an exhibition game against the <a href="/wiki/2008_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2008 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a> on March 28, 2008 at the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Memorial_Coliseum" title="Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum">Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum</a> in honor of the Dodgers 50th anniversary, with 115,300 fans in attendance. All proceeds from the game benefited the official charity of the Dodgers, <a href="/w/index.php?title=ThinkCure!&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="ThinkCure! (page does not exist)">ThinkCure!</a> which supports cancer research at <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Hospital_Los_Angeles" title="Children&#39;s Hospital Los Angeles">Children\'s Hospital Los Angeles</a> and <a href="/wiki/City_of_Hope_National_Medical_Center" title="City of Hope National Medical Center">City of Hope</a>. Primarily Dodgers fans are from their own location in southern California and also parts of southern <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>; however there are also strong pockets of Dodger support in Mexico and throughout Asia, and their away games throughout the US will usually attract substantial numbers of expat and traveling fans.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_and_television">Radio and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Radio and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_broadcasters" title="List of Los Angeles Dodgers broadcasters">List of Los Angeles Dodgers broadcasters</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:VinScully0308.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/VinScully0308.jpg/170px-VinScully0308.jpg" width="170" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/VinScully0308.jpg/255px-VinScully0308.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/VinScully0308.jpg/340px-VinScully0308.jpg 2x" data-file-width="709" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:VinScully0308.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hall of Fame Dodgers broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Vin_Scully" title="Vin Scully">Vin Scully</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Vin_Scully" title="Vin Scully">Vin Scully</a> had called Dodgers games from 1950 to 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-Vin_Scully_Retrospective_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vin_Scully_Retrospective-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> His longtime partners were <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Doggett" title="Jerry Doggett">Jerry Doggett</a> (1956\xe2\x80\x931987) and <a href="/wiki/Ross_Porter_(American_broadcaster)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ross Porter (American broadcaster)">Ross Porter</a> (1977\xe2\x80\x932004).<sup id="cite_ref-Vin_Scully_Retrospective_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vin_Scully_Retrospective-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In 1976, he was selected by Dodgers fans as the Most Memorable Personality (on the field or off) in the team\'s history. He is also a recipient of the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">Baseball Hall of Fame</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Ford_C._Frick_Award" title="Ford C. Frick Award">Ford C. Frick Award</a> for broadcasters (inducted in 1982). Unlike the modern style in which multiple sportscasters have an on-air conversation (usually with one functioning as <a href="/wiki/Play-by-play" class="mw-redirect" title="Play-by-play">play-by-play announcer</a> and the other[s] as <a href="/wiki/Color_commentator" title="Color commentator">color commentator</a>), Scully, Doggett and Porter generally called games solo, trading with each other inning-by-inning. In the 1980s and 1990s, Scully would call the entire radio broadcast except for the third and seventh inning, allowing the other Dodger commentators to broadcast an inning.\n</p><p>When Doggett retired after the 1987 season, he was replaced by Hall-of-Fame Dodgers pitcher <a href="/wiki/Don_Drysdale" title="Don Drysdale">Don Drysdale</a>, who previously broadcast games for the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels_of_Anaheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim">California Angels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vin_Scully_Retrospective_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vin_Scully_Retrospective-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Drysdale died in his hotel room following a heart attack before a game in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a> in 1993. This was a difficult broadcast for Scully and Porter who could not mention it on-air until Drysdale\'s family had been notified and the official announcement made.<sup id="cite_ref-Dodgers&#39;_Death_Brings_out_the_Best_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dodgers&#39;_Death_Brings_out_the_Best-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> He was replaced by former Dodgers outfielder <a href="/wiki/Rick_Monday" title="Rick Monday">Rick Monday</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vin_Scully_Retrospective_41-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vin_Scully_Retrospective-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Porter\'s tenure ended after the 2004 season, after which the format of play-by-play announcers and color commentators was installed, led by Monday and newcomer <a href="/wiki/Charley_Steiner" title="Charley Steiner">Charley Steiner</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vin_Scully_Retrospective_41-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vin_Scully_Retrospective-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Scully, however, continued to announce solo.\n</p><p>Scully called roughly 100 games per season (all home games and road games in California and Arizona)<sup id="cite_ref-Vin_Scully_trims_&#39;12_travel_schedule_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vin_Scully_trims_&#39;12_travel_schedule-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> for both <a href="/wiki/Flagship" title="Flagship">flagship</a> radio station <a href="/wiki/KLAC_(AM)" class="mw-redirect" title="KLAC (AM)">KLAC</a> and on television for <a href="/wiki/SportsNet_LA" class="mw-redirect" title="SportsNet LA">SportsNet LA</a>. Scully was <a href="/wiki/Simulcast" title="Simulcast">simulcast</a> for the first three innings of each of his appearances, then announced only for the TV audience. If Scully was calling the game, Steiner took over play-by-play on radio beginning with the fourth inning, with Monday as color commentator.<sup id="cite_ref-Vin_Scully_trims_&#39;12_travel_schedule_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vin_Scully_trims_&#39;12_travel_schedule-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> If Scully was not calling the game, Steiner and <a href="/wiki/Orel_Hershiser" title="Orel Hershiser">Orel Hershiser</a> called the entire game on television while Monday and Kevin Kennedy did the same on radio. In the event the Dodgers were in post-season play, Scully called the first three and last three innings of the radio broadcast alone and Steiner and Monday handled the middle innings.<sup id="cite_ref-Charley_Steiner_will_do_radio_only_for_the_Dodgers_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charley_Steiner_will_do_radio_only_for_the_Dodgers-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Vin Scully retired from calling games in 2016. His tenure with the Dodgers was the longest with any single sports team at 67 years. Youthful announcer Joe Davis was selected in 2017 by Dodgers management to handle play by play on television with Orel Hershiser as his colorman.\n</p><p>The Dodgers also broadcast on radio in Spanish, and the play-by-play is voiced by another Frick Award winner, <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Jarr%C3%ADn" title="Jaime Jarr\xc3\xadn">Jaime Jarr\xc3\xadn</a>, who has been with the Dodgers since 1959. The color analyst for some games is former Dodger pitcher <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Valenzuela" title="Fernando Valenzuela">Fernando Valenzuela</a>, for whom Jarrin once translated post-game interviews. The Spanish-language radio flagship station is <a href="/wiki/KTNQ_(AM)" class="mw-redirect" title="KTNQ (AM)">KTNQ</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Management">Management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_owners_and_executives" title="List of Los Angeles Dodgers owners and executives">List of Los Angeles Dodgers owners and executives</a></div>\n<ul><li><b>Owner</b>: <a href="/wiki/Guggenheim_Baseball_Management" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sandy_Koufax.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Sandy_Koufax.jpg/170px-Sandy_Koufax.jpg" width="170" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Sandy_Koufax.jpg/255px-Sandy_Koufax.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Sandy_Koufax.jpg/340px-Sandy_Koufax.jpg 2x" data-file-width="961" data-file-height="1213" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sandy_Koufax.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hall of Famer <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Koufax" title="Sandy Koufax">Sandy Koufax</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Koufax, Campanella, and Robinson were the first Dodgers to have their numbers retired, in a ceremony at Dodger Stadium on June 4, 1972. This was the year in which Koufax was inducted into the Baseball Hall of Fame; Robinson and Campanella were already Hall-of-Famers.\n</p><p>Alston\'s number was retired in the year following his retirement as the Dodgers manager, six years before he was inducted into the Hall of Fame.\n</p><p>Gilliam died suddenly in 1978 after a 28-year career with the Dodgers organization. The Dodgers retired his number two days after his death, prior to Game 1 of the <a href="/wiki/1978_World_Series" title="1978 World Series">1978 World Series</a>. As of 2018, he is the only non-Hall-of-Famer to have his number retired by the Dodgers (Alston\'s number was retired before he was elected to the Hall of Fame).\n</p><p>Beginning in 1980, the Dodgers have retired the numbers of longtime Dodgers (Snider, Reese, Drysdale, Lasorda, and Sutton) during the seasons in which each was inducted into the Hall of Fame.\n</p><p>In 1997, 50 years after he broke the <a href="/wiki/Baseball_color_line" title="Baseball color line">color barrier</a> and 25 years after the Dodgers retired his number, Robinson\'s No.42 was retired throughout Major League Baseball. Robinson is the only major league baseball player to have this honor bestowed upon him. Starting in the 2007 season, <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson_Day" title="Jackie Robinson Day">Jackie Robinson Day</a> (April 15, commemorating Opening Day of Robinson\'s rookie season of 1947) has featured many or all players and coaches wearing the number 42 as a tribute to Robinson.\n</p><p>The Dodgers have not issued the number <b>34</b> since the departure of <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Valenzuela" title="Fernando Valenzuela">Fernando Valenzuela</a> in 1991, although it has not been officially retired.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers_award_winners_and_league_leaders" title="Los Angeles Dodgers award winners and league leaders">Los Angeles Dodgers award winners and league leaders</a></div>\n<h3><span
