2012\xe2\x80\x93present</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Managers">Managers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Managers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_managers" title="List of Los Angeles Dodgers managers">List of Los Angeles Dodgers managers</a></div>\n<p>Since 1884, the Dodgers have used a total of 31 Managers, the most current being <a href="/wiki/Dave_Roberts_(outfielder)" title="Dave Roberts (outfielder)">Dave Roberts</a>, who was appointed following the 2015 postseason, after the departure of <a href="/wiki/Don_Mattingly" title="Don Mattingly">Don Mattingly</a>.\n</p><p>Over the nearly 43 years from 1954 to mid-1996, the Dodgers employed only two managers, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Alston" title="Walter Alston">Walter Alston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Lasorda" title="Tommy Lasorda">Tommy Lasorda</a>, both of whom are in the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">Hall of Fame</a>. During this entire time period of extraordinary stability, the Dodgers were family owned by <a href="/wiki/Walter_O%27Malley" title="Walter O&#39;Malley">Walter O\'Malley</a> and then his son <a href="/wiki/Peter_O%27Malley" title="Peter O&#39;Malley">Peter O\'Malley</a>. It was during this era that the Dodgers won 11 of their 21 pennants, and all six of their World Series championships.\n</p><p>The managers of the Los Angeles Dodgers (1958\xe2\x80\x93present) are as follows:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Walter_Alston" title="Walter Alston">Walter Alston</a> (1958\xe2\x80\x931976) (in Brooklyn since 1954)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tommy_Lasorda" title="Tommy Lasorda">Tommy Lasorda</a> (1976\xe2\x80\x931996)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bill_Russell_(baseball)" title="Bill Russell (baseball)">Bill Russell</a> (1996\xe2\x80\x931998)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Glenn_Hoffman" title="Glenn Hoffman">Glenn Hoffman</a> (1998)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Davey_Johnson" title="Davey Johnson">Davey Johnson</a> (1999\xe2\x80\x932000)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jim_Tracy_(baseball)" title="Jim Tracy (baseball)">Jim Tracy</a> (2001\xe2\x80\x932005)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Grady_Little" title="Grady Little">Grady Little</a> (2006\xe2\x80\x932007)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Joe_Torre" title="Joe Torre">Joe Torre</a> (2008\xe2\x80\x932010)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Don_Mattingly" title="Don Mattingly">Don Mattingly</a> (2011\xe2\x80\x932015)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dave_Roberts_(outfielder)" title="Dave Roberts (outfielder)">Dave Roberts</a> (2016\xe2\x80\x93present)</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General_Managers">General Managers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: General Managers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Larry_MacPhail" title="Larry MacPhail">Larry MacPhail</a> (1938\xe2\x80\x931942)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Branch_Rickey" title="Branch Rickey">Branch Rickey</a> (1943\xe2\x80\x931950)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Buzzie_Bavasi" title="Buzzie Bavasi">Buzzie Bavasi</a> (1950\xe2\x80\x931968)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fresco_Thompson" title="Fresco Thompson">Fresco Thompson</a> (1968)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Al_Campanis" title="Al Campanis">Al Campanis</a> (1968\xe2\x80\x931987)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fred_Claire" title="Fred Claire">Fred Claire</a> (1987\xe2\x80\x931998)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tommy_Lasorda" title="Tommy Lasorda">Tommy Lasorda</a> (1998)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kevin_Malone_(baseball)" title="Kevin Malone (baseball)">Kevin Malone</a> (1999\xe2\x80\x932001)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dave_Wallace_(baseball)" title="Dave Wallace (baseball)">Dave Wallace</a> (2001)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dan_Evans_(baseball)" title="Dan Evans (baseball)">Dan Evans</a> (2001\xe2\x80\x932004)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Paul_DePodesta" title="Paul DePodesta">Paul DePodesta</a> (2004\xe2\x80\x932005)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ned_Colletti" title="Ned Colletti">Ned Colletti</a> (2005\xe2\x80\x932014)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Farhan_Zaidi" title="Farhan Zaidi">Farhan Zaidi</a> (2014\xe2\x80\x93present)</li></ul>\n<h3><span id="Public_address_announcers.2Forganists"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_address_announcers/organists">Public address announcers/organists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Public address announcers/organists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>From the Dodgers\' move to Los Angeles from Brooklyn in 1958, the Dodgers employed a handful of well-known public address announcers; the most famous of which was <a href="/wiki/John_Ramsey_(announcer)" title="John Ramsey (announcer)">John Ramsey</a>, who served as the PA voice of the Dodgers from 1958 until his retirement in 1982; as well as announcing at other venerable Los Angeles venues, including the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Memorial_Coliseum" title="Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum">Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Memorial_Sports_Arena" title="Los Angeles Memorial Sports Arena">Sports Arena</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/The_Forum_(Inglewood,_California)" title="The Forum (Inglewood, California)">Forum</a>. Ramsey died in 1990.\n</p><p>From 1958 to 1982, Doug Moore, a local businessman; Philip Petty, an Orange County Superior Court Judge; and Dennis Packer; served as back-up voices for John Ramsey for the Dodgers, California Angels, Los Angeles Chargers, USC football and Los Angeles Rams. Packer was Ramsey\'s primary backup for the Los Angeles Lakers and Los Angeles Kings until Ramsey\'s retirement from the Forum in 1978. Thereafter, Packer became the public address announcer for the Lakers, Kings, indoor soccer and indoor tennis events at the Forum.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nick_Nickson" title="Nick Nickson">Nick Nickson</a>, a radio broadcaster for the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings" title="Los Angeles Kings">Los Angeles Kings</a>, replaced John Ramsey as the Dodger Stadium public address announcer in 1983 and served in that capacity through the 1989 season to work with the Kings full-time.\n</p><p>Dennis Packer and Pete Arbogast were emulators of John Ramsey, using the same stentorian style of announcing Ramsey was famous for. Packer and Arbogast shared the stadium announcing chores for the 1994 FIFA World Cup matches at the Rose Bowl. Arbogast won the Dodgers job on the day that Ramsey died on January 25, 1990, by doing a verbatim imitation of Ramsey\'s opening and closing remarks that were standard at each game. His replacement, in 1993 was <a href="/wiki/Mike_Carlucci" title="Mike Carlucci">Mike Carlucci</a>, who remained as the Dodgers\' PA voice announcer until 2001 to concentrate on his voiceover and acting career along with his Olympics announcing duties.\n</p><p>From 2002 to 2014, the Dodgers public address announcer was Eric Smith, who also announces for the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Clippers" title="Los Angeles Clippers">Los Angeles Clippers</a> and <a href="/wiki/USC_Trojans" title="USC Trojans">USC Trojans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On April 3, 2015 the Dodgers announced that former radio broadcaster <a href="/w/index.php?title=Todd_Leitz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Todd Leitz (page does not exist)">Todd Leitz</a> was hired to become their new public address announcer. Leitz was an anchor and news reporter in Los Angeles at KNX 1070 AM for 10 years, and a news reporter at KABC 790 for two years.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During their time in Brooklyn, stadium organist <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gladys_Gooding&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gladys Gooding (page does not exist)">Gladys Gooding</a> became so well known that fans would joke that she was "the only Dodger who played every game without an error". Gooding was replaced by Helen Dell. From 1988  <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Bea" title="Nancy Bea">Nancy Bea</a> enjoyed a similar level of popularity behind the Dodger Stadium keyboard similar to Gooding\xe2\x80\x99s.\n</p><p>Upon her retirement in 2015, her replacement and current organist is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dieter_Ruehle&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dieter Ruehle (page does not exist)">Dieter Ruehle</a>, who also plays at <a href="/wiki/Staples_Center" title="Staples Center">Staples Center</a> for <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings" title="Los Angeles Kings">Los Angeles Kings</a> games.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Dodgers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Vin_Scully" title="Vin Scully">Vin Scully</a> is permanently honored in the Hall\'s "Scribes &amp; Mikemen" exhibit as a result of winning the <a href="/wiki/Ford_C._Frick_Award" title="Ford C. Frick Award">Ford C. Frick Award</a> in 1982. As with all Frick Award recipients, he is not officially considered an inducted member of the Hall of Fame.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sue_Falsone" title="Sue Falsone">Sue Falsone</a>, served as the first female physical therapist in Major League baseball, and from 2012 to 2013, was the first female head <a href="/wiki/Athletic_trainer" title="Athletic trainer">athletic trainer</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Minor_league_affiliations">Minor league affiliations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
